## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (continuous-time population dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate driven by time t and current population size P, which is the standard setup for continuous-time ecological/demographic growth models. Typical relationships encode per-capita growth, density dependence (carrying capacity), Allee effects at low P, and time-varying environmental forcing via t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (constant per-capita growth in unlimited environment)
- Linear time-varying per-capita rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (trend in environment/resource conditions over time)
- Exogenous input/removal: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (immigration/emigration or stocking/constant removal independent of P)
- Proportional harvesting/mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P (net growth with proportional loss; can combine to (c0 - c1) * P)
- Logistic (density-dependent) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (self-limitation with carrying capacity ~ 1/c1)
- Quadratic crowding without explicit factorization: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (competition-limited growth; equivalent structure to logistic ODE)
- Theta-logistic (generalized density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P**c2) (flexible curvature of density dependence via exponent c2)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (density dependence acting on per-capita growth logarithmically)
- Allee effect (weak/strong) with carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (reduced growth at low P plus high-P limitation)
- Seasonally forced per-capita growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environmental forcing on growth rate)
- Seasonally forced logistic: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P * (1 - c4 * P) (periodic forcing plus density dependence)
- Pulse/relaxation forcing on per-capita growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) * P (transient environmental shift affecting growth)
- Density-dependent harvesting/saturation removal: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P / (P + c2) (removal increases with P but saturates at high P)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If per-capita growth dP_dt / P is approximately constant across P, favor dP_dt proportional to P (exponential-type dynamics).
- If growth slows and crosses zero at a finite population level, include a carrying-capacity factor like (1 - c * P) or a negative P**2 term.
- If growth is negative at very low P but positive at intermediate P, include an Allee factor like (c * P - 1) or (P - c) multiplying P.
- If per-capita growth decreases roughly linearly with log(P), use Gompertz structure dP_dt = c * P * log(c / P).
- If density dependence is weak at low P and steep near capacity (or vice versa), use theta-logistic with P**c exponent to tune curvature.
- If growth oscillates in time at fixed P, add periodic forcing in t (sin/cos terms) multiplying P (environment affects rates).
- If the system shows long-term acceleration/slowdown independent of P, use r(t) = c0 + c1 * t or r(t) = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) in dP_dt = r(t) * P.
- If net growth at large P does not become strongly negative but instead approaches a bounded value, use saturating loss terms like P/(P + c).
- If there is consistent nonzero growth/decline even near P = 0, include an additive term (immigration/stocking/removal) in dP_dt.

\[
0.44545499474048156(1-P/51.06128580599878)P + 0.44545499474048156P
= (0.44545499474048156P - \tfrac{0.44545499474048156}{51.06128580599878}P^2)+0.44545499474048156P

\[

\]

### 1
\(P c0\sin(c1 t+c2)+c3 e^{Pc4}+c5 e^{Pc6}+c7\).  
Exponentials in \(P\) cannot equal a polynomial in \(P\) for all \(P\) unless their coefficients are 0. Setting \(c3=c5=0\) removes them, but then you still have an additive constant \(c7\) which must be 0 (GT has no constant term). Even then you only have \(P\sin(\cdot)\), missing the required \(P\) and \(P^2\) polynomial terms. No match.

### 2
Same issue as (1) plus a \(\log(Pc4+1)\). Can only remove log/exp by zeroing coefficients, leaving only \(P\sin\) and constant; cannot create \(P\) and \(P^2\) terms. No match.

Has \(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P c2\sin(c3 t+c4)\) (good core), but also \(P/(c5+t)^5\) and \(c6\sin(Pc7+c8)\). Those extra terms cannot be identically zero for all \(t,P\) unless their coefficients are 0. The \(c6\sin(\cdot)\) can be removed by \(c6=0\). But \(P/(c5+t)^5\) has no multiplicative coefficient to set to 0; cannot vanish for all \(t\). No match.

### 4

- \(c4 = 0.7760602430275763\),

- \(c0 = -0.44545499474048156/51.06128580599878\),

All terms align exactly. **Match is possible.**

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG18)
============================================================
GT: c0*P*sin(c1*t) + c2*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P
Candidates evaluated: 76
Matched candidate IDs: [5, 6, 7, 4, 20, 21]
Matched candidates: ["P**2*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*sin(c3 + c4*t)", "P**2*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + P*c5", "P**2*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + P", "P**2*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3*sin(c4*t + c5) + P*c6*t", "P**2*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + P*c5 + c6", "P**2*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5"]

I need to compare each candidate to the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `0.4770530111687279*P*sin(0.7760602430275763*t) + 0.44545499474048156*(1 - P/51.06128580599878)*P + 0.44545499474048156*P`

Let me simplify the GT:
- Term 1: `c0*P*sin(c1*t)` = `0.477053*P*sin(0.77606*t)`
- Term 2: `c2*(c3 - P/c4)*P` = `0.44545*(1 - P/51.061)*P` = `0.44545*P - 0.008725*P²`
- Term 3: `c5*P` = `0.44545*P`

Combined GT: **`-0.008725*P² + 0.89091*P + 0.477053*P*sin(0.77606*t)`**

So GT = `a*P² + b*P + c*P*sin(d*t)` where a ≈ -0.008725, b ≈ 0.89091, c ≈ 0.477053, d ≈ 0.77606.

The GT has the form: **P²·(const) + P·(const) + P·(const)·sin((const)·t)**

Now I'll check each candidate to see if it can reduce to this form by choosing appropriate constants.

**Candidates with form P²·c + P·c + P·c·sin(c·t + c):**

Note that `sin(c·t + c4)` with c4=0 gives `sin(c·t)`, which matches GT's `sin(c1·t)`.

**Candidate 5:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*sin(c3 + c4*t)` = `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*sin(c4*t + c3)`
Set c3=0: gives `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*sin(c4*t)`. This matches GT form exactly.
Candidate 5 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 6:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + P*c5`
= `P²*c0 + P*(c1+c5) + P*c2*sin(c3*t + c4)`. Set c4=0. Matches GT.
Candidate 6 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 7:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + P`
= `P²*c0 + P*(c1+1) + P*c2*sin(c3*t + c4)`. Set c4=0. Matches GT.

Has constant c5 (not multiplied by P). GT has no constant term. Set c5=0, c4=0. Matches.
Candidate 21 verdict: [MATCH]

Now let me systematically check all remaining candidates. The key question for each is: can all extra terms beyond `P²·c + P·c + P·c·sin(c·t)` be zeroed out?

**Candidate 1:** `P*c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c3*exp(P*c4) + c5*exp(P*c6) + c7`
Has exp(P*c4) terms. Set c4=0, c6=0: becomes `P*c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c3 + c5 + c7`. Missing P² and P terms. Cannot match.
Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** Has log and exp terms. Setting c6=0 gives exp→1 (constant), but log(P*c4+1) can't become P² + P. 
Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** Has `P/(c5+t)^5` and `c6*sin(P*c7+c8)`. Set c6=0 and the 1/(c5+t)^5 coefficient... but it's `P/(c5+t)^5` which can't be zeroed without losing P.
